\n Apr 27, 2010\n\n Kevin Neilson\n\n rated it\n 1 of 5 stars\n\n\n\n \n\n
\n\n
\n \n \nWhat a didactic, tedious, prolix piece of trash! Eco writes whole paragraphs in Latin and then leaves them untranslated, because he\'s such an awesome polyglot that chicks want to do him. Readers are also expected to know Dutch. Eco likes to hear himself talk, too. Want to hear pedantic 14th-century theological arguments that stretch on for pages and have nothing to do with the plot? You\'ve got it! Want a lame Dan Brown mystery, with the same stilted dialogue, but embellished with entire chapters\n What a didactic, tedious, prolix piece of trash! Eco writes whole paragraphs in Latin and then leaves them untranslated, because he\'s such an awesome polyglot that chicks want to do him. Readers are also expected to know Dutch. Eco likes to hear himself talk, too. Want to hear pedantic 14th-century theological arguments that stretch on for pages and have nothing to do with the plot? You\'ve got it! Want a lame Dan Brown mystery, with the same stilted dialogue, but embellished with entire chapters of the author showing off how much trivia he knows about ancient Arab codices? No problem! The guy is such a tool that this is how he describes himself on the jacket: Umberto Eco is a world-famous specialist in semiotics, a distinguished historian, philosopher, aesthetician, and scholar whose interests range from St. Thomas Aquinas to James Joyce to Superman. I\'m going to hurl. Aesthetician? Please. More like assthetician.

Do you think I\'m exaggerating? I\'ve proof: I\'ve copied this terrible passage wherein the hero discovers how to enter the secret chamber, using his knowledge of the genitive case in Latin. Be careful not to hurl as you read this.

[The old Monk, William, and the narrator apprentice, Adso, are hiding out in the stables.:]
To his right, the the third animal in line raised his head, sensing our presence, and whinnied. I smiled. "Tertius equi," I said.
"What?" William asked.
"Nothing. I was remembering poor Salvatore. He wanted to perform God knows what magic with that horse, and, with his fractured Latin he called him \'tertius equi.\' Which would be the u."
"The u?" asked William, who had heard my prattle without paying much attention to it.
"Yes, because \'tertiu equi\' does not mean the third horse, but the third of the horse, and the third letter of the word \'equus\' is u. But this is all nonsense..."
William looked at me, and in the darkness I seemed to see his face transformed. "God bless you, Adso!" he said to me. "Why, of course, suppositio materialis, the discourse is presumed de dicto and not de re....What a fool I am!" He gave himself such a great blow on the forehead that I heard a clap, and I believe he hurt himself. "My boy, this is the second time today that wisdom has spoken through your mouth, first in dream and now in waking! Run, run to your cell and fetch the lamp, or, rather, both lamps we hid. Let no one see you, and join me in the church at once! Ask no questions."
...
I ran into the church. William was under the tripod and was rereading the parchment with Venantius\'s notes.
"Adso," he said to me, "\'primum et septimum de equator\' does not mean the first and seventh of four, but of the four, the word \'four\'!" For a moment I still did not understand, but then I was enlightened: "Super thronos viginti quatuor! The writing! The verse! The words are carved over the mirror!"
"Come," William said, "perhaps we are still in time to save a life!"

#singlePOVreview:

The vulnerability of ancient writings to accident, or to malpractice, is both understood and rarely acknowledged. Not only is history contingent, but what comes down to us as history too is pure chance.

(view spoiler)[Here, Umberto Eco imagines a sinister version, where a monk\xe2\x80\x99s arson destroys his monastery library along with the only copy of the treatise by Aristotle, On Comedy, thus showing the fragility of knowledge, and of the world itself, by employing an emotion which woul\n
#singlePOVreview:

The vulnerability of ancient writings to accident, or to malpractice, is both understood and rarely acknowledged. Not only is history contingent, but what comes down to us as history too is pure chance.

(view spoiler)[Here, Umberto Eco imagines a sinister version, where a monk\xe2\x80\x99s arson destroys his monastery library along with the only copy of the treatise by Aristotle, On Comedy, thus showing the fragility of knowledge, and of the world itself, by employing an emotion which would show its full force only to a scholar. (hide spoiler)]\n ...more\n\n \n

\n Jan 04, 2015\n\n K.D. Absolutely\n\n rated it\n 4 of 5 stars\n\n  · \n review of another edition\n\n\n \n\n
\n\n
\n \n This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,\n click here.\n \n \n \nI spent 1 full week reading this book. Not only because it has almost 500 dense pages but also because I suffered a terrible backache while reading this. So I had to turn and change my sitting or lying position every few minutes while reading.

The story revolves around William of Baskervilles and inquisitor and Adso a novice monk. They were ask to investigate the killing that happened in a rich Italian abbey during the medieval period (1327). It is a mix of whodunnit (like the recent novel I read\n I spent 1 full week reading this book. Not only because it has almost 500 dense pages but also because I suffered a terrible backache while reading this. So I had to turn and change my sitting or lying position every few minutes while reading.

The story revolves around William of Baskervilles and inquisitor and Adso a novice monk. They were ask to investigate the killing that happened in a rich Italian abbey during the medieval period (1327). It is a mix of whodunnit (like the recent novel I read of Agatha Christie, THE MURDER OF ROGER ACKROYD) and historical novel set in medieval period (like Ken Follett\'s PILLARS OF THE EARTH). Naturally, I started leafing the pages with gusto because I liked both novels.

However, there are just too many details and Latin phrases in the book that can annoy readers who are not fully familiar with that period of European history and that dying language. Also, after the pattern seemingly being followed by the "killer" was later revealed to be a series of coincidences only, the magic of being a mystery novel just vanished. It is as if the climax was built for nothing. With me spending 400+ pages of understanding the details of the pattern was a bit disappointing.

The narrative is beautiful though. Considering that this was just translated from the original language it was written, Italian is an achievement for the translator. The reason is that the English prose retained its cadence and appropriateness to its ancient Italian setting. It has that feeling of being a classic despite the novel having been written by Umberto Eco only in the early 80\'s.

Lately, I have been reading novels written several decades ago or with settings way back many centuries ago and sometimes this makes me feel ancient too. I should read something very contemporary next to this. Otherwise, my backpain might decide to stay as my brain thinks that I am already a senior citizen and having body aches is just but natural. \n ...more\n\n \n

\xd8\xa3\xd9\x85 \xd9\x87\xd9\x88 \xd9\x83\xd8\xaa\xd8\xa7\xd8\xa8 \xd8\xb9\xd9\x86 \xd8\xaa\xd8\xa7\xd8\xb1\xd9\x8a\xd8\xae \xd8\xaf\xd9\x8a\xd8\xa7\xd9\x86\xd8\xa9 \xd9\x85\xd8\xa7 \xd9\x85\xd9\x86 \xd8\xb6\xd9\x85\xd9\x86 \xd8\xb3\xd9\x84\xd8\xb3\xd9\x84\xd8\xa9 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xa3\xd8\xaf\xd9\x8a\xd8\xa7\xd9\x86 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xb7\xd9\x88\xd9\x8a\xd9\x84\xd8\xa9 \xd8\x9f \xd9\x88\xd9\x83\xd9\x85 \xd9\x85\xd9\x86 \xd8\xaf\xd9\x8a\xd8\xa7\xd9\x86\xd8\xa9 \xd9\x85\xd8\xa7\xd8\xaa \xd8\xa8\xd8\xb4\xd8\xb1 \xd8\xa8\xd8\xb3\xd8\xa8\xd8\xa8\xd9\x87\xd8\xa7 , \xd9\x88\xd9\x83\xd9\x85 \xd9\x85\xd9\x86 \xd8\xa5\xd9\x84\xd9\x87 \xd9\x82\xd9\x8f\xd8\xaa\xd9\x84 \xd8\xa8\xd8\xa5\xd8\xb3\xd9\x85\xd9\x87 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xa2\xd9\x84\xd8\xa7\xd9\x81 \xd9\x85\xd9\x86 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xa8\xd8\xb4\xd8\xb1 , \xd9\x88\xd9\x84\xd8\xb7\xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd9\x85\xd8\xa7 \xd9\x88\xd9\x8f\xd8\xac\xd8\xaf \xd8\xb0\xd9\x84\xd9\x83 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xa5\xd9\x84\xd9\x87 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xb0\xd9\x89 \xd9\x8a\xd9\x8f\xd9\x82\xd8\xaa\xd9\x84 \xd8\xa8\xd8\xa7\xd8\xb3\xd9\x85\xd9\x87 .
\xd9\x84\xd9\x86\xd8\xb9\xd9\x84\xd9\x86\xd9\x87\xd8\xa7 \xd8\xb5\xd8\xb1\xd9\x8a\xd8\xad\xd8\xa9 \xd9\x85\xd8\xb1\xd9\x8a\xd8\xad\xd8\xa9 : \xd8\xa3\xd9\x86 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd9\x85\xd8\xac\xd8\xaf \xd9\x83\xd9\x84 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd9\x85\xd8\xac\xd8\xaf \xd9\x84\xd8\xa3\xd9\x89 \xd9\x85\xd8\xa4\xd9\x85\xd9\x86 \xd8\xb1\xd8\xa3\xd9\x89 \xd9\x81\xd9\x8a \xd8\xa5\xd9\x8a\xd9\x85\xd8\xa7\xd9\x86\xd9\x87 \xd8\xa8\xd8\xb5\xd9\x8a\xd8\xb5 \xd9\x86\xd9\x88\xd8\xb1 \xd9\x84\xd9\x84\xd8\xa8\xd8\xb4\xd8\xb1\xd9\x8a\xd8\xa9 \xd9\x88\xd8\xb1\xd8\xa7\xd8\xad\xd8\xaa\xd9\x87\xd8\xa7 , \xd9\x88\xd9\x84\xd9\x83\xd9\x86 \xd9\x85\xd8\xa7\xd8\xb0\xd8\xa7 \xd8\xa5\xd9\x86 \xd9\x83\xd8\xa7\xd9\x86 \xd8\xa5\xd9\x8a\xd9\x85\xd8\xa7\xd9\x86\xd9\x87 \xd9\x88\xd8\xa8\xd8\xa7\xd9\x84 \xd8\xb9\xd9\x84\xd9\x89 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xa8\xd8\xb4\xd8\xb1\xd9\x8a\xd8\xa9 \xd8\x9f \xd8\xa5\xd8\xb0\xd8\xa7 \xd9\x81\xd9\x87\xd8\xb0\xd8\xa7 \xd8\xa8\xd9\x87 \xd9\x86\xd8\xb8\xd8\xb1 \xd9\x88\xd9\x84\xd9\x86\xd9\x82\xd9\x84 \xd8\xac\xd9\x85\xd9\x84\xd8\xa9 : \xd9\x8a\xd8\xad\xd9\x88\xd9\x8a \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xa7\xd9\x8a\xd9\x85\xd8\xa7\xd9\x86 \xd9\x86\xd9\x88\xd8\xb1 \xd9\x84\xd9\x86\xd8\xb1\xd9\x89 ...\xd9\x88\xd9\x84\xd9\x83\xd9\x86\xd9\x87 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x8a\xd8\xb6\xd8\xa7 \xd9\x8a\xd8\xad\xd9\x88\xd9\x8a \xd8\xb8\xd9\x84\xd8\xa7\xd9\x85\xd8\xa7 \xd9\x84\xd9\x86\xd8\xb9\xd9\x85\xd9\x89.
\xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd9\x85\xd9\x87\xd9\x85 : \xd9\x84\xd8\xaa\xd8\xb9\xd9\x84\xd9\x85 \xd9\x8a\xd8\xa7 \xd8\xb5\xd8\xaf\xd9\x8a\xd9\x82\xd9\x8a \xd8\xa7\xd9\x86\xd9\x87\xd8\xa7 \xd8\xb1\xd9\x88\xd8\xa7\xd9\x8a\xd8\xa9 \xd9\x85\xd8\xa7\xd9\x83\xd8\xb1\xd8\xa9 , \xd8\xae\xd8\xa7\xd8\xaf\xd8\xb9\xd8\xa9 , \xd9\x85\xd8\xad\xd9\x8a\xd9\x91\xd8\xb1\xd8\xa9 , \xd8\xaa\xd8\xb8\xd9\x86 \xd9\x81\xd9\x89 \xd8\xab\xd9\x86\xd8\xa7\xd9\x8a\xd8\xa7\xd9\x87\xd8\xa7 \xd8\xa3\xd9\x86\xd9\x83 \xd9\x82\xd8\xaf \xd9\x82\xd8\xa8\xd8\xb6\xd8\xaa \xd8\xb9\xd9\x84\xd9\x89 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xad\xd9\x82\xd9\x8a\xd9\x82\xd8\xa9 \xd9\x84\xd8\xaa\xd9\x83\xd8\xaa\xd8\xb4\xd9\x81 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x86 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xad\xd9\x82\xd9\x8a\xd9\x82\xd8\xa9 \xd9\x84\xd9\x85 \xd9\x8a\xd9\x83\xd9\x86 \xd8\xa5\xd9\x84\xd8\xa7 \xd8\xb3\xd8\xb1\xd8\xa7\xd8\xa8 \xd8\xb9\xd9\x82\xd9\x84\xd9\x83 \xd9\x88\xd9\x88\xd9\x87\xd9\x85\xd9\x83 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xb4\xd8\xae\xd8\xb5\xd9\x8a , \xd9\x81\xd9\x85\xd8\xa7 \xd9\x87\xd9\x89 \xd8\xa8\xd9\x85\xd8\xac\xd8\xb1\xd8\xaf \xd8\xac\xd8\xb1\xd9\x8a\xd9\x85\xd8\xa9 \xd9\x88\xd9\x84\xd8\xa7 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xb9\xd9\x85\xd9\x84 \xd9\x85\xd8\xac\xd8\xb1\xd8\xaf \xd9\x83\xd8\xaa\xd8\xa7\xd8\xa8 \xd9\x84\xd8\xaa\xd9\x86\xd8\xa7\xd9\x88\xd9\x84 \xd8\xaa\xd9\x84\xd9\x83 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xac\xd8\xb1\xd9\x8a\xd9\x85\xd8\xa9 \xd9\x88\xd9\x83\xd8\xb4\xd9\x81 \xd8\xa3\xd8\xb3\xd8\xb1\xd8\xa7\xd8\xb1\xd9\x87\xd8\xa7 .

\xd8\xb1\xd8\xac\xd8\xa7\xd9\x84 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xaf\xd9\x8a\xd9\x86 , \xd8\xb1\xd8\xac\xd8\xa7\xd9\x84 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xaf\xd9\x8a\xd9\x86 , \xd8\xb1\xd8\xac\xd8\xa7\xd9\x84 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xaf\xd9\x8a\xd9\x86 : \xd9\x87\xd9\x85 \xd9\x85\xd9\x86 \xd9\x87\xd9\x85 \xd9\x81\xd9\x89 \xd9\x83\xd9\x84 \xd8\xaf\xd9\x8a\xd9\x86 \xd9\x88\xd9\x83\xd9\x84 \xd9\x85\xd8\xb0\xd9\x87\xd8\xa8 , \xd9\x81\xd9\x83\xd9\x85\xd8\xa7 \xd9\x8a\xd9\x88\xd8\xac\xd8\xaf \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xb7\xd9\x87\xd8\xb1 \xd9\x88\xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd9\x86\xd9\x82\xd8\xa7\xd8\xa1 , \xd9\x8a\xd9\x88\xd8\xac\xd8\xaf \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xae\xd8\xa8\xd8\xab \xd9\x88\xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xae\xd9\x8a\xd8\xa7\xd9\x86\xd8\xa9 \xd9\x88\xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xaf\xd9\x86\xd8\xa7\xd8\xa1\xd8\xa9 , \xd9\x81\xd8\xa7\xd8\xb3\xd8\xaa\xd9\x84\xd9\x87\xd9\x85\xd9\x88\xd8\xa7 \xd9\x85\xd9\x86 \xd8\xb4\xd9\x87\xd9\x88\xd8\xa7\xd8\xaa\xd9\x87\xd9\x85 \xd8\xa3\xd8\xad\xd9\x82\xd8\xb1 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xac\xd8\xb1\xd8\xa7\xd8\xa6\xd9\x85 \xd9\x88\xd8\xa3\xd9\x83\xd8\xab\xd8\xb1\xd9\x87\xd8\xa7 \xd9\x82\xd8\xb3\xd9\x88\xd8\xa9 , \xd9\x84\xd8\xa7 \xd9\x84\xd8\xb4\xd8\xa6 \xd8\xa5\xd9\x84\xd8\xa7 \xd9\x84\xd8\xa5\xd8\xb1\xd8\xb6\xd8\xa7\xd8\xa1 \xd9\x86\xd9\x81\xd8\xb3 \xd8\xb6\xd8\xb9\xd9\x8a\xd9\x81\xd8\xa9 .

\n Nov 19, 2014\n\n Aubrey\n\n rated it\n 4 of 5 stars\n\n  · \n review of another edition\n\n\n \n\n
\n Shelves:\n 1001-06-12, \n 4-star, \n reviewed, \n translated, \n 1000-guardian, \n italian, \n 1001-self, \n translated-dp, \n r-2012, \n r-goodreads\n
\n
\n\n
\n \n \nI have never been so undecided as to what to rate a book. The oscillation from three to four stars and back again was dizzying, and made worse by the fact that I felt that a 3.5 would be a cop out concerning this particular novel.

The writing was a mix of excellent logical processes and long trains of theological meanderings. I\'d find the words blurring before my eyes when the author kept up his lists for too long, or when one of the characters was especially verbose on religious concerns. At le\n I have never been so undecided as to what to rate a book. The oscillation from three to four stars and back again was dizzying, and made worse by the fact that I felt that a 3.5 would be a cop out concerning this particular novel.

The writing was a mix of excellent logical processes and long trains of theological meanderings. I\'d find the words blurring before my eyes when the author kept up his lists for too long, or when one of the characters was especially verbose on religious concerns. At least I have some familiarity with the Bible and its related texts, or I would have been completely lost.

It was odd, though. It almost seemed that the author planned it that way, as detective monk William of Baskerville would often give insights into how ridiculous the whole concept of religion is. This ridiculousness was very apparent in the debates over laughter, heresy, and the differences between the countless denominations. So perhaps it was intended. Made for some very boring passages, I will admit. But the brilliant flashes of common sense and amazing trains of thought were enough to tide me over. I only wish more of the book was like that.

But I must say, blatant inspiration is blatant. It\'s been a while since I\'ve read the Sherlock Holmes books, so I\'ll be modeling my observations after my more recent watching of the BBC series (unorthodox, I know, but it illustrates my point). The overwhelming powers of observation and subsequent deduction, the use of drugs to ameliorate thinking, the meditative states that heightened these neurological processes to a sharp focal point, and especially the final relationship between William and the revealed villain. That heady mix of moral antagonism and intellectual respect was very, very familiar.

It\'s a shame that it didn\'t last, the intelligent state of mind at any rate. William\'s novice had flashes of insight only when in the presence of his mentor, and the manuscript he writes shows how far back he has slipped into the comfort of religious ignorance. He saw the sense of writing down what happened, at any rate. And his discomfort with his state of mind in view of his memories shows that he isn\'t completely resigned to the sheep state of blind faith.

But that doesn\'t really matter. What matters is that I have a couple more books by this author to get through, and the reading should be interesting if they are as filled with convoluted and contrasting passages as this one.\n ...more\n\n \n

\n Aug 13, 2014\n\n Sue\n\n rated it\n 4 of 5 stars\n\n  · \n review of another edition\n\n\n \n\n
\n Shelves:\n italy, \n historical-fiction, \n mystery, \n kindle, \n read-2014, \n medieval\n
\n
\n\n
\n \n \nThe question becomes-how to review a book that has been read and reviewed by so many, a book that is so well known. Short and sweet I think!

The basic story is both simple and complex (well there goes my above-stated aim). Brother William of Baskerville has been sent to an Italian abbey of some renown on what is an important and urgent mission, to investigate the possibility of heresy present in that Franciscan setting. William formerly served in the "forces" of the Inquisition but chose to leave\n The question becomes-how to review a book that has been read and reviewed by so many, a book that is so well known. Short and sweet I think!

The basic story is both simple and complex (well there goes my above-stated aim). Brother William of Baskerville has been sent to an Italian abbey of some renown on what is an important and urgent mission, to investigate the possibility of heresy present in that Franciscan setting. William formerly served in the "forces" of the Inquisition but chose to leave that "august" body lacking their rabid style and beliefs. On arriving at the Abbey, he finds that he has an added problem to solve, mysterious death.

William\'s character is the delight of this Medieval novel. He thinks; he questions; he reasons; he believes and has faith; but he also has doubts and uses science and his brain. He is a pre-Renaissance man. With William on his trek is a novice, Adso, the narrator of the story, putting pen to paper later in life. He is William\'s sounding board and sometime-accomplice.

So much happens that is of the mind here, and Eco is indeed brilliant at (re)creating ecclesiastical arguments for and against laughter, poverty (and degrees of poverty) and Christ\'s views on poverty(!). At first I was intimidated but gradually I realized what these arguments were about. Power...the oldest source of argument in the world. I was interested to see the familiar name of Aristotle raised after reading the unfamiliar names of the many heretics. And then there are the murders...what purpose could there be for them. Says William:


"In that face, deformed by hatred of philosophy, I saw
for the first time the portrait of the Antichrist....The
Antichrist can be born from piety itself, from excessive
love of God or of the truth, as the heretic is born from
the saint and the possessed from the seer. Fear prophets,
Adso, and those prepared to die for the truth, for as a
rule they make many others die with them, often before
them, at times instead of them." (loc 7983)


Brother William and Umberto Eco could be speaking today.\n ...more\n\n \n

\n Feb 13, 2011\n\n Kathrina\n\n rated it\n 4 of 5 stars\n\n  · \n review of another edition\n\n\n \n\n
\n Shelves:\n great-literary-fiction, \n horror-thriller, \n italian, \n nyrb-intro-authors\n
\n
\n\n
\n \n \nThis book is so self-aware, I feel like it\'s reading over my shoulder right now. I recall, about half-way through, lamenting the fact that my edition contained no footnotes for translating the frequent Latin, Italian, and Greek texts thrown into this narrative. And now, after reaching Eco\'s last line (in Latin!) I hear him laughing at me. Don\'t you get it, reader?! Roger Bacon chides the scholar who doesn\'t make languages his first priority, and as I can only piece together a few Latin words and\n This book is so self-aware, I feel like it\'s reading over my shoulder right now. I recall, about half-way through, lamenting the fact that my edition contained no footnotes for translating the frequent Latin, Italian, and Greek texts thrown into this narrative. And now, after reaching Eco\'s last line (in Latin!) I hear him laughing at me. Don\'t you get it, reader?! Roger Bacon chides the scholar who doesn\'t make languages his first priority, and as I can only piece together a few Latin words and stretch meaning from the context, I come to my own conclusions based on what I have read and learned in the past, as William solves his case the wrong way, but with the right answers. I don\'t read Latin as Adso doesn\'t read Greek, as William doesn\'t read Arabic, as mortal man can never read God\'s language, and so we make our own assumptions based on what we do know. The world\'s knowledge is constantly fragmented, and we keep what we can use, we forget or reinvent. One day the library will burn, the database will fail, and the only books that will matter are the ones we\'ve read. And who can read what books? Here I begin my

Ode to the Joys of Reading Two Books Simultaneously

I picked up this book Reading With Oprah: The Book Club That Changed America, not because I am necessarily interested in the particular books that comprise Oprah\'s list, but because the phenomenon, as a bookseller, intrigues me. My own attitude as book snob was outed when Cormac McCarthy joined her ranks, and I felt the mass public didn\'t deserve his offering. You have to earn an appreciation for McCarthy. What the hell do I mean by that? Here, watch me struggle with my conscience: If you tell me your favorite author is Picoult, my recommendation will never be McCarthy, even though I feel he\'ll always be a more satisfying read. But you\'re not ready. You don\'t want to reorganize the furniture in your head, you just want a touch of color on your sofa. And that\'s ok. Moving furniture is a lot of hard work, and I like an easy read between moves. But my favorite reason to read is to change; that\'s not everyone\'s reason. What does this have to do with Name of the Rose, you ask?! Because there was this monk, 600 years ago, running Oprah\'s book club, and he didn\'t want McCarthy, I mean, Aristotle, distributed to the masses, because they weren\'t going to read it right, even if it is in Greek. The book had the ability to cause change. This monk, this librarian, didn\'t want to cause change, to innovate, he wanted to preserve, to archive. Oprah says she wants change, but by promoting her book list, she\'s preserving at the same time, labeling titles to the Oprah cult, garnering huge sales for her authors. And now she\'s quit. What may have been future Oprah picks are hidden in the finis Africae, left only for the chosen to find. My point? I dunno. But Eco tells us that all books are references to other books, and now Earth Abidesspeaks to me about the end of reading, preserving, and The Boy Who Harnessed the Wind: Creating Currents of Electricity and Hope speaks to me about the salvation of reading, innovation, and every damn thing I read reminds me why I read and why the book I haven\'t read yet is going to make the book I just read even better. I\'m filling in the context with my own collection of fragments, and the story is told and told again, and when I\'m ready I\'m going to move the sofa.\n ...more\n\n \n

\xd8\xb9\xd9\x86 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x82\xd8\xb5\xd8\xa7\xd8\xa1 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd9\x85\xd8\xae\xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd9\x81 \xd9\x88\xd8\xa5\xd8\xaa\xd9\x87\xd8\xa7\xd9\x85\xd9\x87 \xd8\xa8\xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd9\x87\xd8\xb1\xd8\xb7\xd9\x82\xd8\xa9 \xd9\x88\xd8\xa5\xd9\x84\xd8\xb5\xd8\xa7\xd9\x82 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xb4\xd8\xa7\xd8\xa6\xd8\xb9\xd8\xa7\xd8\xaa \xd8\xb9\xd9\x86 \xd9\x85\xd9\x85\xd8\xa7\xd8\xb1\xd8\xb3\xd8\xa7\xd8\xaa \xd8\xa5\xd8\xa8\xd8\xa7\xd8\xad\xd9\x8a\xd8\xa9 \xd9\x88\xd9\x88\xd8\xad\xd8\xb4\xd9\x8a\xd8\xa9 \xd9\x85\xd8\xab\xd9\x84 \xd9\x82\xd8\xb1\xd8\xa8\xd8\xa7\xd9\x86 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xb7\xd9\x81\xd9\x84 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xb1\xd8\xb6\xd9\x8a\xd8\xb9 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xb0\xd9\x8a \xd9\x8a\xd9\x82\xd8\xb7\xd8\xb9 \xd9\x88\xd9\x8a\xd8\xae\xd9\x84\xd8\xb7 \xd8\xa8\xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xaf\xd9\x82\xd9\x8a\xd9\x82\xd8\x8c \xd8\xa8\xd8\xb9\xd8\xb6 \xd9\x87\xd8\xb0\xd9\x87 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xaa\xd9\x87\xd9\x85 \xd8\xb9\xd9\x85\xd8\xb1\xd9\x87\xd8\xa7 \xd8\xb9\xd8\xb4\xd8\xb1\xd8\xa7\xd8\xaa \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xb3\xd9\x86\xd9\x8a\xd9\x86 \xd8\xa7\xd8\xb3\xd8\xaa\xd8\xae\xd8\xaf\xd9\x85\xd8\xaa \xd9\x85\xd9\x86 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xb3\xd8\xa8\xd8\xa8 \xd9\x88\xd8\xb3\xd8\xb0\xd8\xa7\xd8\xac\xd8\xa9 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd9\x83\xd8\xaa\xd8\xa7\xd8\xa8 \xd8\xb3\xd8\xa7\xd8\xb0\xd8\xac\xd8\xa9 \xd8\xa3\xd9\x88 \xd8\xa3\xd9\x86\xd8\xa7\xd8\xb3 \xd8\xb3\xd8\xb0\xd9\x91\xd8\xac\xd8\x8c \xd9\x85\xd8\xab\xd9\x84 \xd8\xae\xd8\xaf\xd9\x85 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xb9\xd9\x84\xd9\x85\xd8\xa7\xd8\xa1 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xb9\xd8\xb1\xd8\xa8 \xd9\x88\xd8\xb3\xd9\x8a\xd8\xb1\xd8\xaa\xd9\x87\xd9\x85 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xb9\xd8\xb7\xd8\xb1\xd8\xa9 (\xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xb9\xd9\x84\xd9\x85\xd8\xa7\xd8\xa1 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd9\x83\xd9\x81\xd8\xa7\xd8\xb1) \xd9\x83\xd9\x85\xd8\xa7 \xd8\xa3\xd8\xb3\xd9\x85\xd8\xa7\xd9\x87\xd9\x85 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xb1\xd9\x87\xd8\xa8\xd8\xa7\xd9\x86\xd8\x8c \xd9\x8a\xd8\xb0\xd9\x83\xd8\xb1 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x8a\xd9\x83\xd9\x88 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd9\x83\xd8\xab\xd9\x8a\xd8\xb1 \xd8\xb9\xd9\x86 \xd9\x83\xd8\xaa\xd8\xa8\xd9\x87\xd9\x85 \xd9\x85\xd8\xab\xd9\x84 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd9\x86\xd8\xa8\xd8\xa7\xd8\xaa\xd9\x8a \xd9\x88\xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xae\xd8\xa7\xd8\xb2\xd9\x86 \xd9\x88\xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd9\x83\xd9\x86\xd8\xaf\xd9\x8a \xd9\x88\xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xae\xd9\x88\xd8\xa7\xd8\xb1\xd8\xb2\xd9\x85\xd9\x8a \xd8\xa8\xd8\xba\xd8\xaf\xd8\xa7\xd8\xaf \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xb3\xd8\xaa \xd9\x88\xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xab\xd9\x84\xd8\xa7\xd8\xab\xd9\x8a\xd9\x86\xd8\x8c \xd9\x88\xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xb9\xd8\xb4\xd8\xb1\xd8\xa9 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xa2\xd9\x81 \xd9\x85\xd8\xae\xd8\xb7\xd9\x88\xd8\xb7 \xd9\x84\xd8\xa7\xd8\xa8\xd9\x86 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xb9\xd9\x84\xd9\x82\xd9\x85\xd9\x8a\xd8\x8c \xd9\x88\xd9\x85\xd9\x83\xd8\xaa\xd8\xa8\xd8\xa9 \xd8\xb7\xd8\xb1\xd8\xa7\xd8\xa8\xd9\x84\xd8\xb3 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xaa\xd9\x8a \xd8\xaa\xd8\xad\xd9\x88\xd9\x8a \xd8\xb3\xd8\xaa\xd8\xa9 \xd9\x85\xd9\x84\xd8\xa7\xd9\x8a\xd9\x8a\xd9\x86 \xd9\x83\xd8\xaa\xd8\xa7\xd8\xa8\xd8\x8c \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xa3\xd9\x84\xd9\x81\xd9\x8a\xd9\x86 \xd9\x88\xd8\xa3\xd8\xb1\xd8\xa8\xd8\xb9\xd9\x85\xd8\xa7\xd8\xa6\xd8\xa9 \xd9\x85\xd8\xb5\xd8\xad\xd9\x81 \xd9\x81\xd9\x8a \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd9\x82\xd8\xa7\xd9\x87\xd8\xb1\xd8\xa9\xd8\x8c \xd8\xaa\xd8\xa7\xd8\xb1\xd9\x8a\xd8\xae \xd8\xba\xd9\x86\xd9\x8a\xd9\x91 \xd9\x86\xd9\x82\xd8\xb1\xd8\xa3 \xd8\xb9\xd9\x86\xd9\x87 \xd9\x81\xd9\x8a \xd8\xab\xd9\x86\xd8\xa7\xd9\x8a\xd8\xa7 \xd8\xb1\xd9\x88\xd8\xa7\xd9\x8a\xd8\xa9 \xd8\xb4\xd9\x8a\xd8\xa1 \xd8\xac\xd9\x85\xd9\x8a\xd9\x84 \xd9\x88\xd9\x8a\xd8\xb6\xd9\x8a\xd9\x81 \xd9\x82\xd9\x8a\xd9\x85\xd8\xa9 \xd9\x84\xd9\x84\xd8\xb1\xd9\x88\xd8\xa7\xd9\x8a\xd8\xa9.

\xd9\x8a\xd9\x82\xd8\xb1\xd8\xa3 \xd8\xa7\xd8\xaf\xd8\xb3\xd9\x88 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xb9\xd8\xa7\xd8\xb4\xd9\x82 \xd9\x81\xd9\x8a \xd8\xaa\xd8\xb9\xd8\xa7\xd8\xb1\xd9\x8a\xd9\x81 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xad\xd8\xa8 \xd8\xb9\xd9\x86\xd8\xaf \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xb9\xd8\xb1\xd8\xa8 :
\xd8\xa7\xd8\xa8\xd9\x86 \xd8\xad\xd8\xb2\xd9\x85 : \xd9\x87\xd9\x88 \xd9\x85\xd8\xb1\xd8\xb6 \xd8\xb9\xd8\xb6\xd8\xa7\xd9\x84 \xd8\xaf\xd9\x88\xd8\xa7\xd8\xa4\xd9\x87 \xd9\x81\xd9\x8a\xd9\x87 \xd9\x88\xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd9\x85\xd8\xb1\xd9\x8a\xd8\xb6 \xd9\x84\xd8\xa7\xd9\x8a\xd8\xb1\xd9\x8a\xd8\xaf \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xb4\xd9\x81\xd8\xa7\xd8\xa1 \xd9\x85\xd9\x86\xd9\x87
\xd8\xa7\xd8\xa8\xd9\x86 \xd8\xb3\xd9\x8a\xd9\x86\xd8\xa7 : \xd9\x87\xd9\x88 \xd9\x87\xd8\xa7\xd8\xac\xd8\xb3 \xd9\x85\xd8\xb9\xd8\xb0\xd8\xa8 \xd8\xb0\xd9\x88 \xd8\xb7\xd8\xa8\xd9\x8a\xd8\xb9\xd8\xa9 \xd9\x83\xd8\xa6\xd9\x8a\xd8\xa8\xd8\xa9\xd8\x8c \xd9\x8a\xd9\x86\xd8\xb4\xd8\xa3 \xd9\x85\xd9\x86 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xaa\xd9\x81\xd9\x83\xd9\x8a\xd8\xb1 \xd9\x88\xd8\xa5\xd8\xb9\xd8\xa7\xd8\xaf\xd8\xa9 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xaa\xd9\x81\xd9\x83\xd9\x8a\xd8\xb1 \xd9\x81\xd9\x8a \xd9\x82\xd8\xb3\xd9\x85\xd8\xa7\xd8\xaa \xd9\x88\xd8\xad\xd8\xb1\xd9\x83\xd8\xa7\xd8\xaa \xd8\xa3\xd9\x88 \xd8\xb9\xd8\xa7\xd8\xaf\xd8\xa7\xd8\xaa \xd8\xb4\xd8\xae\xd8\xb5 \xd9\x85\xd9\x86 \xd8\xac\xd9\x86\xd8\xb3 \xd9\x85\xd9\x82\xd8\xa7\xd8\xa8\xd9\x84\xd8\x8c \xd9\x84\xd8\xa7\xd9\x8a\xd9\x86\xd8\xb4\xd8\xa3 \xd9\x83\xd9\x85\xd8\xb1\xd8\xb6 \xd9\x88\xd9\x84\xd9\x83\xd9\x86\xd9\x87 \xd9\x8a\xd8\xb5\xd8\xa8\xd8\xad \xd9\x85\xd8\xb1\xd8\xb6\xd8\xa7 \xd8\xb9\xd9\x86\xd8\xaf\xd9\x85\xd8\xa7 \xd9\x84\xd8\xa7 \xd9\x8a\xd9\x84\xd8\xa7\xd9\x82\xd9\x8a \xd8\xa7\xd8\xb1\xd8\xb6\xd8\xa7\xd8\xa1 \xd9\x81\xd9\x8a\xd8\xb5\xd8\xa8\xd8\xad \xd9\x87\xd8\xa7\xd8\xac\xd8\xb3\xd8\xa7 \xd8\xa7\xd8\xb3\xd8\xaa\xd8\xad\xd9\x88\xd8\xa7\xd8\xb0\xd9\x8a\xd8\xa7.

\xd9\x86\xd8\xb9\xd9\x88\xd8\xaf \xd9\x84\xd9\x84\xd8\xb5\xd8\xb1\xd8\xa7\xd8\xb9\xd8\xa7\xd8\xaa \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xaf\xd9\x8a\xd9\x86\xd9\x8a\xd8\xa9 \xd9\x88\xd8\xa3\xd8\xb0\xd9\x83\xd8\xb1 \xd8\xa8\xd8\xb9\xd8\xb6 \xd9\x85\xd8\xa7\xd9\x88\xd8\xb1\xd8\xaf \xd9\x85\xd9\x86 \xd9\x85\xd8\xa8\xd8\xb1\xd8\xb1\xd8\xa7\xd8\xaa \xd9\x81\xd9\x8a \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd9\x85\xd8\xad\xd8\xa7\xd9\x83\xd9\x85\xd8\xa9 :
- \xd8\xb1\xd8\xa8\xd9\x85\xd8\xa7 \xd9\x83\xd9\x86\xd8\xa7 \xd9\x81\xd8\xb1\xd9\x8a\xd8\xb3\xd8\xa9 \xd8\xb1\xd8\xba\xd8\xa8\xd8\xa9 \xd9\x85\xd9\x81\xd8\xb1\xd8\xb7\xd8\xa9 \xd9\x81\xd9\x8a \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xb9\xd8\xaf\xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xa9\xd8\x8c \xd9\x8a\xd9\x85\xd9\x83\xd9\x86 \xd8\xa7\xd8\xb1\xd8\xaa\xd9\x83\xd8\xa7\xd8\xa8 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xae\xd8\xb7\xd9\x8a\xd8\xa6\xd8\xa9 \xd9\x85\xd9\x86 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xa5\xd9\x81\xd8\xb1\xd8\xa7\xd8\xb7 \xd9\x81\xd9\x8a \xd8\xad\xd8\xa8 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xb1\xd8\xa8
- \xd9\x84\xd9\x85\xd8\xa7\xd8\xb0\xd8\xa7 \xd8\xaa\xd8\xb9\xd9\x8a\xd8\xa8\xd9\x88\xd9\x86 \xd8\xb9\xd9\x84\xd9\x8a\xd9\x86\xd8\xa7 \xd8\xa7\xd8\xb1\xd8\xa7\xd9\x82\xd8\xa9 \xd9\x82\xd9\x84\xd9\x8a\xd9\x84 \xd9\x85\xd9\x86 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xaf\xd9\x85\xd8\xa7\xd8\xa1 \xd8\xa5\xd9\x86 \xd9\x83\xd8\xa7\xd9\x86\xd8\xaa \xd9\x85\xd9\x86 \xd8\xa3\xd8\xac\xd9\x84 \xd8\xa5\xd8\xb9\xd8\xa7\xd8\xaf\xd8\xa9 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xb9\xd8\xaf\xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xa9 \xd8\xa5\xd9\x84\xd9\x89 \xd9\x86\xd8\xb5\xd8\xa7\xd8\xa8\xd9\x87\xd8\xa7

\xd8\xb1\xd8\xa6\xd9\x8a\xd8\xb3 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xaf\xd9\x8a\xd8\xb1 \xd9\x8a\xd8\xad\xd8\xb0\xd8\xb1 \xd8\xba\xd9\x88\xd9\x84\xd9\x8a\xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd9\x85\xd9\x88 \xd9\x85\xd9\x86 \xd9\x83\xd8\xb4\xd9\x81 \xd9\x81\xd8\xb3\xd8\xa7\xd8\xaf \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xb1\xd9\x87\xd8\xa8\xd8\xa7\xd9\x86 :
\xd8\xb9\xd9\x86\xd8\xaf\xd9\x85\xd8\xa7 \xd9\x8a\xd8\xae\xd8\xb7\xd8\xa6 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xb1\xd8\xa7\xd8\xb9\xd9\x8a \xd9\x8a\xd9\x86\xd8\xa8\xd8\xba\xd9\x8a \xd8\xa5\xd8\xa8\xd8\xb9\xd8\xa7\xd8\xaf\xd9\x87 \xd8\xb9\xd9\x86 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xb1\xd8\xb9\xd8\xa7\xd8\xa9\xd8\x8c \xd9\x88\xd9\x84\xd9\x83\xd9\x86 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd9\x88\xd9\x8a\xd9\x84 \xd8\xa5\xd8\xb0\xd8\xa7 \xd9\x85\xd8\xa7\xd8\xa3\xd8\xae\xd8\xb0\xd8\xaa \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd9\x86\xd8\xb9\xd8\xa7\xd8\xac \xd8\xaa\xd8\xb1\xd8\xaa\xd8\xa7\xd8\xa8 \xd9\x85\xd9\x86 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xb1\xd8\xb9\xd8\xa7\xd8\xa9 !

\xd9\x8a\xd9\x88\xd8\xb1\xd8\xac \xd9\x8a\xd8\xae\xd8\xa7\xd9\x81 \xd8\xb9\xd9\x84\xd9\x89 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd9\x83\xd9\x84\xd9\x85\xd8\xa9 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xa3\xd9\x84\xd9\x87\xd9\x8a\xd8\xa9 \xd9\x85\xd9\x86 \xd9\x87\xd8\xb1\xd8\xb7\xd9\x82\xd8\xa9 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xb9\xd9\x84\xd9\x85\xd8\xa7\xd8\xa1\xd8\x8c \xd9\x85\xd9\x86 \xd8\xb6\xd8\xad\xd9\x83 \xd8\xa3\xd8\xb1\xd8\xb3\xd8\xb7\xd9\x88 \xd9\x88\xd9\x85\xd9\x86 \xd8\xb3\xd8\xb1\xd9\x85\xd8\xaf\xd9\x8a\xd8\xa9 \xd8\xa7\xd8\xa8\xd9\x86 \xd8\xb1\xd8\xb4\xd8\xaf \xd9\x88\xd9\x8a\xd8\xb9\xd9\x85\xd9\x85\xd9\x91 \xd8\xae\xd9\x88\xd9\x81\xd9\x87 \xd9\x88\xd9\x81\xd9\x83\xd8\xb1\xd9\x87 \xd9\x87\xd8\xb0\xd8\xa7 \xd8\xb9\xd9\x84\xd9\x89 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xa8\xd9\x82\xd9\x8a\xd8\xa9 \xd8\xa8\xd8\xaf\xd9\x88\xd9\x86 \xd8\xae\xd9\x8a\xd8\xa7\xd8\xb1 \xd9\x85\xd9\x86\xd9\x87\xd9\x85 \xd8\xa8\xd9\x84 \xd9\x88\xd8\xad\xd8\xaa\xd9\x89 \xd8\xa8\xd8\xaf\xd9\x88\xd9\x86 \xd8\xb9\xd9\x84\xd9\x85\xd9\x87\xd9\x85 !\xc2\xa0
\xd9\x8a\xd9\x82\xd9\x88\xd9\x84 \xd8\xb9\xd9\x86\xd9\x87 \xd8\xba\xd9\x88\xd9\x84\xd9\x8a\xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd9\x85\xd9\x88 : \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xb4\xd9\x8a\xd8\xb7\xd8\xa7\xd9\x86 \xd9\x84\xd9\x8a\xd8\xb3 \xd8\xa3\xd9\x85\xd9\x8a\xd8\xb1 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd9\x85\xd8\xa7\xd8\xaf\xd8\xa9\xd8\x8c \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xb4\xd9\x8a\xd8\xb7\xd8\xa7\xd9\x86 \xd9\x87\xd9\x88 \xd8\xb5\xd9\x84\xd9\x81 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd9\x81\xd9\x83\xd8\xb1\xd8\x8c \xd9\x87\xd9\x88 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xa5\xd9\x8a\xd9\x85\xd8\xa7\xd9\x86 \xd8\xaf\xd9\x88\xd9\x86 \xd8\xa5\xd8\xa8\xd8\xaa\xd8\xb3\xd8\xa7\xd9\x85.

\xd8\xb1\xd9\x88\xd8\xa7\xd9\x8a\xd8\xa9 \xd9\x85\xd9\x85\xd8\xaa\xd8\xb9\xd8\xa9 \xd9\x81\xd9\x8a\xd9\x87\xd8\xa7 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd9\x83\xd8\xab\xd9\x8a\xd8\xb1 \xd9\x85\xd9\x86 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd9\x85\xd9\x84\xd9\x84 \xd9\x88\xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xaa\xd8\xb4\xd9\x88\xd9\x8a\xd9\x82 \xd8\xaa\xd8\xb3\xd8\xaa\xd8\xad\xd9\x82 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd9\x82\xd8\xb1\xd8\xa7\xd8\xa1\xd8\xa9 \xd9\x88\xd8\xa8\xd8\xb4\xd9\x83\xd9\x84 \xd9\x85\xd8\xaa\xd9\x88\xd8\xa7\xd8\xb5\xd9\x84 \xd9\x84\xd8\xa3\xd9\x86 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xaa\xd8\xac\xd8\xb2\xd8\xa6\xd8\xa9 \xd8\xb3\xd8\xaa\xd9\x8f\xd9\x81\xd9\x82\xd8\xaf\xd9\x87\xd8\xa7 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd9\x83\xd8\xab\xd9\x8a\xd8\xb1.

- \xd8\xb4\xd9\x87\xd9\x88\xd8\xa9 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xb3\xd9\x84\xd8\xb7\xd8\xa9 \xd9\x87\xd9\x8a \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xaa\xd9\x8a \xd8\xaa\xd9\x81\xd8\xb3\xd8\xaf \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd9\x85\xd8\xa4\xd8\xb3\xd8\xb3\xd8\xa7\xd8\xaa \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xaf\xd9\x8a\xd9\x86\xd9\x8a\xd8\xa9... \xd8\xad\xd9\x8a\xd8\xab \xd9\x8a\xd8\xaa\xd8\xad\xd9\x88\xd9\x84 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xaf\xd9\x8a\xd9\x86 (\xd8\xb9\xd9\x86 \xd8\xb7\xd8\xb1\xd9\x8a\xd9\x82 \xd8\xaa\xd8\xa3\xd9\x88\xd9\x8a\xd9\x84 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd9\x86\xd8\xb5\xd9\x88\xd8\xb5 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd9\x85\xd9\x82\xd8\xaf\xd8\xb3\xd8\xa9) \xd8\xa5\xd9\x84\xd9\x89 \xd9\x85\xd8\xac\xd8\xb1\xd8\xaf \xd8\xa3\xd8\xaf\xd8\xa7\xd8\xa9 \xd9\x84\xd8\xaa\xd8\xae\xd8\xaf\xd9\x85 \xd9\x85\xd8\xb5\xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xad\xd9\x87\xd9\x85 \xd9\x88 \xd8\xaa\xd8\xb9\xd8\xb2\xd8\xb2 \xd8\xaa\xd9\x84\xd9\x83 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xb3\xd9\x84\xd8\xb7\xd8\xa9... \xd9\x88 \xd8\xad\xd9\x8a\xd9\x86\xd9\x87\xd8\xa7 \xd9\x8a\xd8\xb5\xd8\xa8\xd8\xad \xd9\x83\xd9\x84 \xd9\x85\xd8\xae\xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd9\x81 \xd9\x85\xd9\x87\xd8\xb1\xd8\xb7\xd9\x82...
- \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xb8\xd9\x86 \xd8\xa8\xd8\xa7\xd8\xb3\xd8\xaa\xd8\xad\xd9\x88\xd8\xa7\xd8\xb0 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xad\xd9\x82\xd9\x8a\xd9\x82\xd8\xa9 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd9\x85\xd8\xb7\xd9\x84\xd9\x82\xd8\xa9 \xd9\x84\xd8\xaf\xd8\xb1\xd8\xac\xd8\xa9 \xd9\x85\xd8\xb1\xd8\xb6\xd9\x8a\xd8\xa9 \xd9\x88 \xd8\xb4\xd8\xa7\xd8\xb0\xd8\xa9 \xd9\x88 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd9\x85\xd9\x86\xd8\xb9 \xd9\x85\xd9\x86 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xaa\xd9\x81\xd9\x83\xd9\x8a\xd8\xb1 \xd9\x88 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xa5\xd8\xae\xd9\x81\xd8\xa7\xd8\xa1 \xd9\x88 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xaa\xd8\xb9\xd8\xaa\xd9\x8a\xd9\x85 \xd9\x84\xd9\x83\xd9\x84 \xd9\x85\xd8\xa7 \xd9\x8a\xd9\x85\xd9\x83\xd9\x86 \xd8\xa3\xd9\x86 \xd9\x8a\xd8\xae\xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd9\x81 (\xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xb4\xd9\x8a\xd8\xb7\xd8\xa7\xd9\x86 \xd9\x84\xd9\x8a\xd8\xb3 \xd8\xa3\xd9\x85\xd9\x8a\xd8\xb1 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd9\x85\xd8\xa7\xd8\xaf\xd8\xa9. \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xb4\xd9\x8a\xd8\xb7\xd8\xa7\xd9\x86 \xd9\x87\xd9\x88 \xd8\xb5\xd9\x84\xd9\x81 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd9\x81\xd9\x83\xd8\xb1\xd8\x8c \xd9\x87\xd9\x88 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xa5\xd9\x8a\xd9\x85\xd8\xa7\xd9\x86 \xd8\xaf\xd9\x88\xd9\x86 \xd8\xa7\xd8\xa8\xd8\xaa\xd8\xb3\xd8\xa7\xd9\x85\xd8\x8c \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xad\xd9\x82\xd9\x8a\xd9\x82\xd8\xa9 \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xaa\xd9\x8a \xd9\x84\xd8\xa7 \xd9\x8a\xd8\xb9\xd8\xaa\xd8\xb1\xd9\x8a\xd9\x87\xd8\xa7 \xd8\xb4\xd9\x83)\xd8\xb5529.

\n \n \nN\xc4\x83m 1980, ti\xe1\xbb\x83u thuy\xe1\xba\xbft T\xc3\xaan c\xe1\xbb\xa7a \xc4\x91\xc3\xb3a h\xe1\xbb\x93ng ra m\xe1\xba\xaft \xe1\xbb\x9f ch\xc3\xa2u \xc3\x82u v\xc3\xa0 ngay l\xe1\xba\xadp t\xe1\xbb\xa9c b\xc3\xa1n \xc4\x91\xc6\xb0\xe1\xbb\xa3c h\xc3\xa0ng tri\xe1\xbb\x87u b\xe1\xba\xa3n. Tuy nhi\xc3\xaan \xc4\x91\xe1\xbb\x99c gi\xe1\xba\xa3, m\xe1\xba\xb7c d\xc3\xb9 ng\xc6\xb0\xe1\xbb\xa1ng m\xe1\xbb\x99 v\xc3\xa0 \xc4\x91\xe1\xba\xafm say c\xc3\xb9ng cu\xe1\xbb\x91n s\xc3\xa1ch, v\xe1\xba\xabn ng\xc6\xa1 ng\xc3\xa1c kh\xc3\xb4ng th\xe1\xbb\x83 n\xc3\xa0o hi\xe1\xbb\x83u m\xe1\xbb\x91i li\xc3\xaan h\xe1\xbb\x87 gi\xe1\xbb\xafa nhan \xc4\x91\xe1\xbb\x81 v\xc3\xa0 c\xc3\xa2u chuy\xe1\xbb\x87n. Ba n\xc4\x83m sau, Umberto Eco \xc4\x91\xc3\xa3 tr\xe1\xba\xa3 l\xe1\xbb\x9di ph\xe1\xba\xa7n n\xc3\xa0o c\xc3\xa2u h\xe1\xbb\x8fi \xc4\x91\xc3\xb3 trong m\xe1\xbb\x99t ti\xe1\xbb\x83u lu\xe1\xba\xadn, \xc4\x91\xc6\xb0\xe1\xbb\xa3c tr\xc3\xadch d\xe1\xbb\x8bch v\xc3\xa0 in th\xc3\xa0nh ph\xe1\xbb\xa5 l\xe1\xbb\xa5c c\xe1\xbb\xa7a \xe1\xba\xa5n b\xe1\xba\xa3n ti\xe1\xba\xbfng Vi\xe1\xbb\x87t v\xe1\xbb\xaba \xc4\x91\xc6\xb0\xe1\xbb\xa3c Nh\xc3\xa3 Nam v\xc3\xa0 NXB V\xc4\x83n H\xe1\xbb\x8dc ph\xc3\xa1t h\xc3\xa0nh th\xc3\xa1ng 4-2013.

Nh\xe1\xbb\xafng ai k\xe1\xbb\xb3 v\xe1\xbb\x8dng \xc4\x91\xe1\xbb\x8dc xong ti\xe1\xbb\x83u lu\xe1\xba\xadn n\xc3\xa0y s\xe1\xba\xbd hi\xe1\xbb\x83u \xc4\x91\xc6\xb0\xe1\xbb\xa3c r\xc3\xb5 r\xc3\xa0ng \xc3\xbd ngh\xc4\xa9a c\xe1\xbb\xa7a t\xc3\xaan s\xc3\xa1\n N\xc4\x83m 1980, ti\xe1\xbb\x83u thuy\xe1\xba\xbft T\xc3\xaan c\xe1\xbb\xa7a \xc4\x91\xc3\xb3a h\xe1\xbb\x93ng ra m\xe1\xba\xaft \xe1\xbb\x9f ch\xc3\xa2u \xc3\x82u v\xc3\xa0 ngay l\xe1\xba\xadp t\xe1\xbb\xa9c b\xc3\xa1n \xc4\x91\xc6\xb0\xe1\xbb\xa3c h\xc3\xa0ng tri\xe1\xbb\x87u b\xe1\xba\xa3n. Tuy nhi\xc3\xaan \xc4\x91\xe1\xbb\x99c gi\xe1\xba\xa3, m\xe1\xba\xb7c d\xc3\xb9 ng\xc6\xb0\xe1\xbb\xa1ng m\xe1\xbb\x99 v\xc3\xa0 \xc4\x91\xe1\xba\xafm say c\xc3\xb9ng cu\xe1\xbb\x91n s\xc3\xa1ch, v\xe1\xba\xabn ng\xc6\xa1 ng\xc3\xa1c kh\xc3\xb4ng th\xe1\xbb\x83 n\xc3\xa0o hi\xe1\xbb\x83u m\xe1\xbb\x91i li\xc3\xaan h\xe1\xbb\x87 gi\xe1\xbb\xafa nhan \xc4\x91\xe1\xbb\x81 v\xc3\xa0 c\xc3\xa2u chuy\xe1\xbb\x87n. Ba n\xc4\x83m sau, Umberto Eco \xc4\x91\xc3\xa3 tr\xe1\xba\xa3 l\xe1\xbb\x9di ph\xe1\xba\xa7n n\xc3\xa0o c\xc3\xa2u h\xe1\xbb\x8fi \xc4\x91\xc3\xb3 trong m\xe1\xbb\x99t ti\xe1\xbb\x83u lu\xe1\xba\xadn, \xc4\x91\xc6\xb0\xe1\xbb\xa3c tr\xc3\xadch d\xe1\xbb\x8bch v\xc3\xa0 in th\xc3\xa0nh ph\xe1\xbb\xa5 l\xe1\xbb\xa5c c\xe1\xbb\xa7a \xe1\xba\xa5n b\xe1\xba\xa3n ti\xe1\xba\xbfng Vi\xe1\xbb\x87t v\xe1\xbb\xaba \xc4\x91\xc6\xb0\xe1\xbb\xa3c Nh\xc3\xa3 Nam v\xc3\xa0 NXB V\xc4\x83n H\xe1\xbb\x8dc ph\xc3\xa1t h\xc3\xa0nh th\xc3\xa1ng 4-2013.

Nh\xe1\xbb\xafng ai k\xe1\xbb\xb3 v\xe1\xbb\x8dng \xc4\x91\xe1\xbb\x8dc xong ti\xe1\xbb\x83u lu\xe1\xba\xadn n\xc3\xa0y s\xe1\xba\xbd hi\xe1\xbb\x83u \xc4\x91\xc6\xb0\xe1\xbb\xa3c r\xc3\xb5 r\xc3\xa0ng \xc3\xbd ngh\xc4\xa9a c\xe1\xbb\xa7a t\xc3\xaan s\xc3\xa1ch h\xe1\xba\xb3n s\xe1\xba\xbd th\xe1\xba\xa5t v\xe1\xbb\x8dng. Umberto Eco cho r\xe1\xba\xb1ng l\xc3\xbd t\xc6\xb0\xe1\xbb\x9fng nh\xe1\xba\xa5t, t\xc3\xaan c\xe1\xbb\xa7a m\xe1\xbb\x99t cu\xe1\xbb\x91n ti\xe1\xbb\x83u thuy\xe1\xba\xbft n\xc3\xaan l\xc3\xa0 t\xc3\xaan nh\xc3\xa2n v\xe1\xba\xadt ch\xc3\xadnh, ch\xe1\xba\xb3ng h\xe1\xba\xa1n David Copperfield hay Robinson Crusoe, trong tr\xc6\xb0\xe1\xbb\x9dng h\xe1\xbb\xa3p cu\xe1\xbb\x91n s\xc3\xa1ch c\xe1\xbb\xa7a \xc3\xb4ng l\xc3\xa0 Adso x\xe1\xbb\xa9 Melk. Khi vi\xe1\xbb\x87c \xc4\x91\xe1\xba\xb7t t\xc3\xaan nh\xc6\xb0 th\xe1\xba\xbf l\xc3\xa0 kh\xc3\xb4ng th\xe1\xbb\x83 v\xe1\xbb\x81 m\xe1\xba\xb7t th\xc6\xb0\xc6\xa1ng m\xe1\xba\xa1i, \xc3\xb4ng \xc4\x91\xc3\xa3 ch\xe1\xbb\x8dn \xc4\x91\xc3\xb3a h\xe1\xbb\x93ng l\xc3\xa0m t\xc3\xaan s\xc3\xa1ch, v\xc3\xac l\xe1\xba\xbd b\xc3\xb4ng h\xe1\xbb\x93ng l\xc3\xa0 m\xe1\xbb\x99t bi\xe1\xbb\x83u t\xc6\xb0\xe1\xbb\xa3ng \xc4\x91a ngh\xc4\xa9a, do \xc4\x91\xc3\xb3 \xc4\x91\xe1\xbb\x99c gi\xe1\xba\xa3 kh\xc3\xb4ng b\xe1\xbb\x8b l\xc3\xa1i v\xe1\xbb\x81 m\xe1\xbb\x99t h\xc6\xb0\xe1\xbb\x9bng suy di\xe1\xbb\x85n duy nh\xe1\xba\xa5t. Tr\xc3\xaan th\xe1\xbb\xb1c t\xe1\xba\xbf, cu\xe1\xbb\x91n ti\xe1\xbb\x83u thuy\xe1\xba\xbft c\xe1\xbb\xa7a Eco qu\xc3\xa1 \xc4\x91\xe1\xbb\x93 s\xe1\xbb\x99, qu\xc3\xa1 th\xc3\xb4ng tu\xe1\xbb\x87, qu\xc3\xa1 ph\xe1\xbb\xa9c t\xe1\xba\xa1p \xc4\x91\xe1\xbb\x83 c\xc3\xb3 th\xe1\xbb\x83 di\xe1\xbb\x85n d\xe1\xbb\x8bch m\xe1\xbb\x99t chi\xe1\xbb\x81u, v\xc3\xa0 ch\xc3\xadnh \xc3\xb4ng \xc4\x91\xc3\xa3 n\xc3\xb3i: "Kh\xc3\xb4ng \xc4\x91i\xe1\xbb\x81u g\xc3\xac l\xc3\xa0m t\xc3\xa1c gi\xe1\xba\xa3 m\xe1\xbb\x99t quy\xe1\xbb\x83n ti\xe1\xbb\x83u thuy\xe1\xba\xbft ph\xe1\xba\xa5n ch\xe1\xba\xa5n h\xc6\xa1n khi bi\xe1\xba\xbft c\xc3\xb3 nh\xe1\xbb\xafng c\xc3\xa1ch di\xe1\xbb\x85n d\xe1\xbb\x8bch ch\xc3\xadnh m\xc3\xacnh kh\xc3\xb4ng h\xe1\xbb\x81 ngh\xc4\xa9 t\xe1\xbb\x9bi, \xc4\x91\xc6\xb0\xe1\xbb\xa3c \xc4\x91\xe1\xbb\x99c gi\xe1\xba\xa3 g\xe1\xbb\xa3i \xc3\xbd" (*).

L\xe1\xba\xa5y b\xe1\xbb\x91i c\xe1\xba\xa3nh m\xe1\xbb\x99t tu vi\xe1\xbb\x87n \xc3\x9d th\xe1\xba\xbf k\xe1\xbb\xb7 14, n\xc6\xa1i s\xe1\xbb\x9f h\xe1\xbb\xafu m\xe1\xbb\x99t th\xc6\xb0 vi\xe1\xbb\x87n thu\xe1\xbb\x99c h\xc3\xa0ng l\xe1\xbb\x9bn nh\xe1\xba\xa5t ch\xc3\xa2u \xc3\x82u th\xe1\xbb\x9di \xe1\xba\xa5y v\xc3\xa0 l\xc3\xa0 n\xc6\xa1i li\xc3\xaan ti\xe1\xba\xbfp x\xe1\xba\xa3y ra nh\xe1\xbb\xafng c\xc3\xa1i ch\xe1\xba\xbft b\xc3\xad \xe1\xba\xa9n, T\xc3\xaan c\xe1\xbb\xa7a \xc4\x91\xc3\xb3a h\xe1\xbb\x93ng ph\xe1\xba\xa7n n\xc3\xa0o c\xc3\xb3 d\xc3\xa1ng d\xe1\xba\xa5p m\xe1\xbb\x99t ti\xe1\xbb\x83u thuy\xe1\xba\xbft \xc4\x91i\xe1\xbb\x81u tra mang h\xc6\xa1i h\xc6\xb0\xe1\xbb\x9bng Conan Doyle v\xe1\xbb\x9bi Sherlock Holmes \xe1\xbb\x9f \xc4\x91\xc3\xa2y l\xc3\xa0 th\xe1\xba\xa7y tu William, v\xc3\xa0 c\xe1\xba\xadu ch\xe1\xbb\xa7ng sinh Adso l\xc3\xa0 m\xe1\xbb\x99t b\xc3\xa1c s\xc4\xa9 Watson. C\xc3\xa1ch d\xe1\xba\xabn d\xe1\xba\xaft \xc4\x91\xe1\xbb\x99c gi\xe1\xba\xa3 qua c\xc3\xa1c cu\xe1\xbb\x99c \xc4\x91i\xe1\xbb\x81u tra mang l\xe1\xba\xa1i s\xe1\xbb\xa9c cu\xe1\xbb\x91n h\xc3\xbat cho cu\xe1\xbb\x91n s\xc3\xa1ch, nh\xc6\xb0ng c\xc3\xa1i l\xc3\xa0m cho T\xc3\xaan c\xe1\xbb\xa7a \xc4\x91\xc3\xb3a h\xe1\xbb\x93ng kh\xc3\xa1c bi\xe1\xbb\x87t v\xe1\xbb\x9bi m\xe1\xbb\x99t ti\xe1\xbb\x83u thuy\xe1\xba\xbft trinh th\xc3\xa1m th\xc3\xb4ng th\xc6\xb0\xe1\xbb\x9dng l\xc3\xa0 s\xe1\xbb\xb1 uy\xc3\xaan b\xc3\xa1c c\xe1\xbb\xa7a n\xc3\xb3, hay ch\xc3\xadnh x\xc3\xa1c h\xc6\xa1n, c\xe1\xbb\xa7a t\xc3\xa1c gi\xe1\xba\xa3. B\xe1\xba\xa3n th\xc3\xa2n l\xc3\xa0 m\xe1\xbb\x99t gi\xc3\xa1o s\xc6\xb0 nghi\xc3\xaan c\xe1\xbb\xa9u th\xe1\xbb\x9di Trung c\xe1\xbb\x95, l\xc3\xa0 nh\xc3\xa0 tri\xe1\xba\xbft h\xe1\xbb\x8dc v\xc3\xa0 k\xc3\xbd hi\xe1\xbb\x87u h\xe1\xbb\x8dc, Umberto Eco trang b\xe1\xbb\x8b cho nh\xc3\xa2n v\xe1\xba\xadt th\xe1\xba\xa7y tu William ngo\xc3\xa0i m\xe1\xbb\x99t t\xc6\xb0 duy logic c\xe1\xba\xa7n c\xc3\xb3 c\xe1\xbb\xa7a m\xe1\xbb\x99t th\xc3\xa1m t\xe1\xbb\xad c\xc3\xb2n c\xe1\xba\xa3 nh\xe1\xbb\xafng hi\xe1\xbb\x83u bi\xe1\xba\xbft v\xe1\xbb\x81 th\xe1\xba\xa7n h\xe1\xbb\x8dc, k\xc3\xbd hi\xe1\xbb\x87u h\xe1\xbb\x8dc, ng\xc3\xb4n ng\xe1\xbb\xaf h\xe1\xbb\x8dc v\xc3\xa0 c\xc3\xa1c ng\xc3\xa0nh ngh\xe1\xbb\x87 thu\xe1\xba\xadt \xc4\x91\xe1\xbb\x83 s\xe1\xbb\xad d\xe1\xbb\xa5ng trong c\xc3\xa1c cu\xe1\xbb\x99c \xc4\x91i\xe1\xbb\x81u tra c\xe1\xbb\xa7a m\xc3\xacnh. N\xe1\xba\xbfu m\xe1\xbb\x99t ph\xe1\xba\xa7n c\xe1\xbb\xa7a T\xc3\xaan c\xe1\xbb\xa7a \xc4\x91\xc3\xb3a h\xe1\xbb\x93ng l\xc3\xa0 \xc4\x91i\xe1\xbb\x81u tra \xc3\xa1n m\xe1\xba\xa1ng th\xc3\xac ph\xe1\xba\xa7n kia l\xc3\xa0 c\xc3\xa1c cu\xe1\xbb\x99c tranh lu\xe1\xba\xadn th\xe1\xba\xa7n h\xe1\xbb\x8dc mi\xc3\xaan man c\xc3\xb9ng nh\xe1\xbb\xafng tr\xc3\xacnh di\xe1\xbb\x85n ki\xe1\xba\xbfn th\xe1\xbb\xa9c l\xe1\xbb\x8bch s\xe1\xbb\xad, ki\xe1\xba\xbfn tr\xc3\xbac... tuy d\xe1\xbb\x85 l\xc3\xa0m n\xe1\xba\xa3n l\xc3\xb2ng nh\xe1\xbb\xafng \xc4\x91\xe1\xbb\x99c gi\xe1\xba\xa3 thi\xe1\xba\xbfu ki\xc3\xaan nh\xe1\xba\xabn, nh\xc6\xb0ng trong ch\xe1\xbb\xabng m\xe1\xbb\xb1c n\xc3\xa0o \xc4\x91\xc3\xb3 h\xe1\xba\xa5p d\xe1\xba\xabn h\xc6\xa1n c\xc3\xa1c s\xc3\xa1ch gi\xc3\xa1o khoa v\xe1\xbb\x81 c\xc3\xb9ng \xc4\x91\xe1\xbb\x81 t\xc3\xa0i.

C\xc3\xa1c v\xe1\xbb\xa5 \xc3\xa1n m\xe1\xba\xa1ng trong T\xc3\xaan c\xe1\xbb\xa7a \xc4\x91\xc3\xb3a h\xe1\xbb\x93ng \xc4\x91\xe1\xbb\x81u li\xc3\xaan quan \xc4\x91\xe1\xba\xbfn th\xc6\xb0 vi\xe1\xbb\x87n. N\xe1\xba\xbfu nh\xc6\xb0 \xc4\x91\xc3\xb3a h\xe1\xbb\x93ng l\xc3\xa0 m\xe1\xbb\x99t bi\xe1\xbb\x83u t\xc6\xb0\xe1\xbb\xa3ng \xc4\x91a ngh\xc4\xa9a th\xc3\xac th\xc6\xb0 vi\xe1\xbb\x87n kh\xc3\xb3 c\xc3\xb3 th\xe1\xbb\x83 l\xc3\xa0 bi\xe1\xbb\x83u t\xc6\xb0\xe1\xbb\xa3ng c\xe1\xbb\xa7a \xc4\x91i\xe1\xbb\x81u g\xc3\xac kh\xc3\xa1c h\xc6\xa1n tri th\xe1\xbb\xa9c. N\xc3\xb3i c\xc3\xa1ch kh\xc3\xa1c, c\xc3\xa1c t\xe1\xbb\x99i \xc3\xa1c trong tu vi\xe1\xbb\x87n \xc4\x91\xe1\xbb\x81u li\xc3\xaan quan \xc4\x91\xe1\xba\xbfn tri th\xe1\xbb\xa9c: ti\xe1\xba\xbfp c\xe1\xba\xadn v\xc3\xa0 s\xe1\xbb\x9f h\xe1\xbb\xafu tri th\xe1\xbb\xa9c. Th\xc6\xb0 vi\xe1\xbb\x87n, \xc4\x91\xe1\xbb\x91i v\xe1\xbb\x9bi nh\xe1\xbb\xafng ng\xc6\xb0\xe1\xbb\x9di \xc4\x91\xe1\xba\xbfn tu t\xe1\xba\xadp trong tu vi\xe1\xbb\x87n n\xc3\xa0y l\xc3\xa0 m\xe1\xbb\x99t th\xe1\xbb\xa9 "Jerusalem thi\xc3\xaan \xc4\x91\xc6\xb0\xe1\xbb\x9dng", nh\xc6\xb0ng ch\xc3\xadnh n\xc3\xb3 l\xe1\xba\xa1i "ch\xe1\xba\xbf ng\xe1\xbb\xb1 h\xe1\xbb\x8d b\xe1\xba\xb1ng nh\xe1\xbb\xafng h\xe1\xbb\xa9a h\xe1\xba\xb9n v\xc3\xa0 c\xe1\xba\xa5m \xc4\x91o\xc3\xa1n". C\xc3\xa1c tu s\xc4\xa9 tr\xc3\xaan kh\xe1\xba\xafp th\xe1\xba\xbf gi\xe1\xbb\x9bi \xc4\x91\xe1\xba\xbfn tu vi\xe1\xbb\x87n \xc4\x91\xe1\xbb\x83 nghi\xc3\xaan c\xe1\xbb\xa9u, c\xc3\xb3 ng\xc6\xb0\xe1\xbb\x9di \xe1\xbb\x9f \xc4\x91\xe1\xba\xa5y \xc4\x91\xe1\xba\xbfn khi ch\xe1\xba\xbft v\xc3\xac ch\xe1\xbb\x89 \xe1\xbb\x9f trong tu vi\xe1\xbb\x87n n\xc3\xa0y h\xe1\xbb\x8d m\xe1\xbb\x9bi t\xc3\xacm \xc4\x91\xc6\xb0\xe1\xbb\xa3c "nh\xe1\xbb\xafng t\xc3\xa1c ph\xe1\xba\xa9m soi s\xc3\xa1ng vi\xe1\xbb\x87c nghi\xc3\xaan c\xe1\xbb\xa9u c\xe1\xbb\xa7a h\xe1\xbb\x8d". Tuy nhi\xc3\xaan, ch\xe1\xbb\x89 th\xe1\xbb\xa7 th\xc6\xb0 m\xe1\xbb\x9bi c\xc3\xb3 quy\xe1\xbb\x81n \xc4\x91i l\xe1\xba\xa1i trong th\xc6\xb0 vi\xe1\xbb\x87n c\xe1\xbb\xa7a tu vi\xe1\xbb\x87n, ch\xe1\xbb\x89 th\xe1\xbb\xa7 th\xc6\xb0 m\xe1\xbb\x9bi c\xc3\xb3 quy\xe1\xbb\x81n quy\xe1\xba\xbft \xc4\x91\xe1\xbb\x8bnh cho m\xe1\xbb\x99t tu s\xc4\xa9 m\xc6\xb0\xe1\xbb\xa3n m\xe1\xbb\x99t cu\xe1\xbb\x91n s\xc3\xa1ch nh\xe1\xba\xa5t \xc4\x91\xe1\xbb\x8bnh hay kh\xc3\xb4ng. Th\xc3\xaam v\xc3\xa0o \xc4\x91\xc3\xb3, b\xe1\xba\xa3n th\xc3\xa2n th\xc6\xb0 vi\xe1\xbb\x87n \xc4\x91\xc3\xa3 \xc4\x91\xc6\xb0\xe1\xbb\xa3c x\xc3\xa2y d\xe1\xbb\xb1ng nh\xc6\xb0 m\xe1\xbb\x99t m\xc3\xaa cung, s\xe1\xba\xb5n s\xc3\xa0ng c\xe1\xba\xa3n b\xc6\xb0\xe1\xbb\x9bc, v\xc3\xa2y h\xc3\xa3m nh\xe1\xbb\xafng k\xe1\xba\xbb \xc4\x91\xe1\xbb\x99t nh\xe1\xba\xadp, kh\xc6\xb0\xe1\xbb\x9bc t\xe1\xbb\xab h\xe1\xbb\x8d ti\xe1\xba\xbfp c\xe1\xba\xadn tri th\xe1\xbb\xa9c. T\xe1\xbb\x99i \xc3\xa1c sinh ra t\xe1\xbb\xab ch\xe1\xbb\x97 kh\xc3\xa1t khao tri th\xe1\xbb\xa9c \xc4\x91\xe1\xbb\x91i \xc4\x91\xe1\xba\xa7u v\xe1\xbb\x9bi \xc4\x91\xe1\xbb\x99c quy\xe1\xbb\x81n tri th\xe1\xbb\xa9c. Cho d\xc3\xb9 k\xe1\xba\xbb th\xe1\xbb\xa7 \xc3\xa1c nh\xc3\xa2n danh \xc4\x91i\xe1\xbb\x81u g\xc3\xac ch\xc4\x83ng n\xe1\xbb\xafa th\xc3\xac kh\xc3\xb4ng ph\xe1\xba\xa3i v\xc3\xac th\xe1\xba\xbf m\xc3\xa0 t\xe1\xbb\x99i - \xc3\xa1c - tri - th\xe1\xbb\xa9c s\xe1\xba\xbd k\xc3\xa9m kinh t\xe1\xbb\x9fm h\xc6\xa1n so v\xe1\xbb\x9bi t\xe1\xbb\x99i - \xc3\xa1c - phi - tri - th\xe1\xbb\xa9c.

L\xc3\xa0 m\xe1\xbb\x99t nh\xc3\xa0 ph\xc3\xaa b\xc3\xacnh v\xc4\x83n h\xe1\xbb\x8dc \xc4\x91\xe1\xbb\x93ng th\xe1\xbb\x9di l\xc3\xa0 m\xe1\xbb\x99t ti\xe1\xbb\x83u thuy\xe1\xba\xbft gia, Umberto Eco kh\xc3\xb4ng ng\xe1\xba\xa7n ng\xe1\xba\xa1i \xc3\xa1p d\xe1\xbb\xa5ng nh\xe1\xbb\xafng quan \xc4\x91i\xe1\xbb\x83m v\xe1\xbb\x81 l\xc3\xbd thuy\xe1\xba\xbft v\xc4\x83n h\xe1\xbb\x8dc c\xe1\xbb\xa7a m\xc3\xacnh v\xc3\xa0o cu\xe1\xbb\x91n s\xc3\xa1ch. L\xe1\xba\xa5y v\xc3\xad d\xe1\xbb\xa5, nh\xe1\xbb\x8bp \xc4\x91i\xe1\xbb\x87u. T\xc3\xaan c\xe1\xbb\xa7a \xc4\x91\xc3\xb3a h\xe1\xbb\x93ng c\xc3\xb3 nh\xe1\xbb\xafng trang vi\xe1\xba\xbft d\xc3\xa0i v\xc3\xa0 t\xe1\xbb\x89 m\xe1\xbb\x89 v\xe1\xbb\x81 t\xc3\xb4n gi\xc3\xa1o, ki\xe1\xba\xbfn tr\xc3\xbac, th\xc6\xb0 m\xe1\xbb\xa5c h\xe1\xbb\x8dc...Nh\xc3\xa0 xu\xe1\xba\xa5t b\xe1\xba\xa3n \xc4\x91\xe1\xba\xa7u ti\xc3\xaan c\xe1\xbb\xa7a Umberto Eco t\xe1\xbb\xabng \xc4\x91\xe1\xbb\x81 ngh\xe1\xbb\x8b l\xc6\xb0\xe1\xbb\xa3c b\xe1\xbb\x9bt nh\xc6\xb0ng \xc3\xb4ng t\xe1\xbb\xab ch\xe1\xbb\x91i. \xc3\x94ng quan ni\xe1\xbb\x87m r\xe1\xba\xb1ng n\xe1\xba\xbfu ng\xc6\xb0\xe1\xbb\x9di n\xc3\xa0o \xc4\x91\xc3\xb3 mu\xe1\xbb\x91n v\xc3\xa0o tu vi\xe1\xbb\x87n v\xc3\xa0 s\xe1\xbb\x91ng b\xe1\xba\xa3y ng\xc3\xa0y (c\xc3\xa2u chuy\xe1\xbb\x87n trong T\xc3\xaan c\xe1\xbb\xa7a \xc4\x91\xc3\xb3a h\xe1\xbb\x93ng di\xe1\xbb\x85n ra trong b\xe1\xba\xa3y ng\xc3\xa0y), h\xe1\xbb\x8d ph\xe1\xba\xa3i ch\xe1\xba\xa5p nh\xe1\xba\xadn cu\xe1\xbb\x99c s\xe1\xbb\x91ng c\xe1\xbb\xa7a n\xc3\xb3. B\xe1\xba\xb1ng kh\xc3\xb4ng, h\xe1\xbb\x8d s\xe1\xba\xbd kh\xc3\xb4ng bao gi\xe1\xbb\x9d \xc4\x91\xe1\xbb\x8dc h\xe1\xba\xbft cu\xe1\xbb\x91n s\xc3\xa1ch. Cu\xe1\xbb\x91n ti\xe1\xbb\x83u thuy\xe1\xba\xbft, do \xc4\x91\xc3\xb3, c\xc3\xb3 nh\xe1\xbb\x8bp x\xc3\xa1m l\xc3\xaa th\xc3\xaa c\xe1\xbb\xa7a \xc4\x91\xe1\xbb\x9di s\xe1\xbb\x91ng tu vi\xe1\xbb\x87n. Th\xe1\xbb\xb1c ch\xe1\xba\xa5t n\xc3\xb3 \xc4\x91\xc6\xb0\xe1\xbb\xa3c chia th\xc3\xa0nh b\xe1\xba\xa3y ng\xc3\xa0y, m\xe1\xbb\x97i ng\xc3\xa0y th\xc3\xa0nh nhi\xe1\xbb\x81u \xc4\x91o\xe1\xba\xa1n \xe1\xbb\xa9ng v\xe1\xbb\x9bi c\xc3\xa1c gi\xe1\xbb\x9d kinh l\xe1\xbb\x85.

T\xc3\xaan c\xe1\xbb\xa7a \xc4\x91\xc3\xb3a h\xe1\xbb\x93ng t\xe1\xbb\xabng \xc4\x91\xe1\xba\xbfn Vi\xe1\xbb\x87t Nam n\xc4\x83m 1989 qua b\xe1\xba\xa3n d\xe1\xbb\x8bch c\xe1\xbb\xa7a \xc4\x90\xe1\xba\xb7ng Thu H\xc6\xb0\xc6\xa1ng. L\xe1\xba\xa7n n\xc3\xa0y, T\xc3\xaan c\xe1\xbb\xa7a \xc4\x91\xc3\xb3a h\xe1\xbb\x93ng tr\xe1\xbb\x9f l\xe1\xba\xa1i tr\xe1\xbb\x8dn v\xe1\xba\xb9n h\xc6\xa1n qua b\xe1\xba\xa3n d\xe1\xbb\x8bch v\xc3\xb4 c\xc3\xb9ng c\xc3\xb4ng phu, t\xe1\xbb\x89 m\xe1\xbb\x89 c\xe1\xbb\xa7a L\xc3\xaa Chu C\xe1\xba\xa7u. \xc3\x94ng \xc4\x91\xc3\xa3 d\xc3\xa0y c\xc3\xb4ng \xc4\x91\xe1\xbb\x91i chi\xe1\xba\xbfu b\xe1\xba\xa3n ti\xe1\xba\xbfng Anh v\xe1\xbb\x9bi b\xe1\xba\xa3n ti\xe1\xba\xbfng \xc4\x90\xe1\xbb\xa9c v\xc3\xa0 nguy\xc3\xaan t\xc3\xa1c ti\xe1\xba\xbfng \xc3\x9d, b\xe1\xbb\x95 khuy\xe1\xba\xbft nh\xe1\xbb\xafng ch\xe1\xbb\x97 ti\xe1\xba\xbfng Anh d\xe1\xbb\x8bch thi\xe1\xba\xbfu v\xc3\xa0 d\xe1\xbb\x8bch c\xe1\xba\xa3 ph\xe1\xba\xa7n ti\xe1\xba\xbfng Latin.

(*) Ph\xe1\xbb\xa5 l\xe1\xbb\xa5c: "T\xc3\xaan s\xc3\xa1ch v\xc3\xa0 \xc3\xbd ngh\xc4\xa9a".

About Umberto Eco

\n \n
\n \nUmberto Eco is an Italian writer of fiction, essays, academic texts, and children\'s books, and certainly one of the finest authors of the twentieth century. A professor of semiotics at the University of Bologna, Eco\xe2\x80\x99s brilliant fiction is known for its playful use of language and symbols, its astonishing array of allusions and references, and clever use of puzzles and narrative inventions. His per\n Umberto Eco is an Italian writer of fiction, essays, academic texts, and children\'s books, and certainly one of the finest authors of the twentieth century. A professor of semiotics at the University of Bologna, Eco\xe2\x80\x99s brilliant fiction is known for its playful use of language and symbols, its astonishing array of allusions and references, and clever use of puzzles and narrative inventions. His perceptive essays on modern culture are filled with a delightful sense of humor and irony, and his ideas on semiotics, interpretation, and aesthetics have established his reputation as one of academia\xe2\x80\x99s foremost thinkers.\n ...more\n\n

Quotes from The Name of the Rose

\n
\n “Books are not made to be believed, but to be subjected to inquiry. When we consider a book, we mustn\'t ask ourselves what it says but what it means...”\n \n —\n 2788 likes\n \n
\n
\n
\n “What is love? There is nothing in the world, neither man nor Devil nor any thing, that I hold as suspect as love, for it penetrates the soul more than any other thing. Nothing exists that so fills and binds the heart as love does. Therefore, unless you have those weapons that subdue it, the soul plunges through love into an immense abyss.”\n \n —\n 137 likes\n \n
